<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:SYMBOL; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

</B>
</FONT>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:14.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:14.667PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	OVERVIEW
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Silver Wheaton Corp. (&#147;Silver Wheaton&#148; or the &#147;Company&#148;) is a growth-oriented silver company, and is the only mining company with 100% of its revenue from silver production. The Company&#146;s goal is to be recognized as the largest, most profitable and best managed pure silver company in the world.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During the four months ended December 31, 2004, Silver Wheaton acquired the rights to purchase all of the silver produced by Goldcorp&#146;s Luismin mines in Mexico, and by Lundin Mining&#146;s Zinkgruvan mine in Sweden (the &#147;Luismin Transaction&#148; and the &#147;Zinkgruvan Transaction&#148; respectively). &nbsp;Both mines are low-cost producers and are expected to have remaining lives of over 20 years.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During August, 2005, the Company acquired approximately 15% of the common shares of Bear Creek Mining Corporation (TSXV: BCM) (&#147;Bear Creek&#148;) for total consideration of $13.7 million (Cdn$16.4 million.)
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 22, 2005, the Company raised gross proceeds of $86.2 million (Cdn$100.0 million) from a private placement of 15,625,000 subscription receipts at a price of Cdn$6.40 per unit. &nbsp;The Company is actively pursuing further growth opportunities either by way of entering into long-term silver purchase contracts, or by acquiring silver exploration, development or production assets.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	1
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage7"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	On February 13, 2006, Silver Wheaton announced that it had agreed to amend its existing silver purchase agreement with Goldcorp, in connection with Goldcorp&#146;s plans to substantially increase its investment in exploration and development at its San Dimas mine in Mexico, resulting in projected additional silver production of more than 100 million ounces over the remaining term of their 25 year agreement. &nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:5PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:5PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On February 23, 2006, Silver Wheaton announced that it has agreed to purchase 4.75 million ounces of silver per year, for a period of 20 years, from Glencore International AG, based on the production from their Yauliyacu mining operations in Per&#250;.&nbsp; With this acquisition, Silver Wheaton is expected to have annual silver sales of over 15 million ounces in 2006 increasing to 20 million ounces by 2009 and thereafter.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:14.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	SILVER WHEATON CORP. RESTATEMENT
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Silver Wheaton is filing this amendment to its Annual Report for the year ended December 31, 2005, to amend and restate the United States Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (&#147;US GAAP&#148;) note disclosure in its financial statements for the year ended December 31, 2005, and the four months ended December 31, 2004. &nbsp;In addition, the Company is filing amendments to its Quarterly Report for the period ended June 30, 2006, to amend and restate the US GAAP note disclosure in its financial statements for the second quarter of 2006. The restatement adjusts the Company&#146;s US GAAP accounting for share purchase warrants with an exercise price denominated in a currency other than the Company&#146;s functional currency, issued by the Company commencing in October 2004. &nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company reports in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles (&#147;Canadian GAAP&#148;) and provides note disclosure in its financial statements with respect to a reconciliation of Canadian GAAP to US GAAP.&nbsp; Under Canadian GAAP, share purchase warrants are accounted for as equity and recorded at their historical cost.&nbsp;Based on an interpretation by US regulatory authorities, of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (&#147;SFAS&#148;) No. 133,
<I>
	Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities
</I>
	, share purchase warrants denominated in a currency other than the functional currency of the Company are classified and accounted for as a financial liability at their fair value with any resulting gains or losses being included in the calculation of US GAAP earnings. &nbsp;In these circumstances, a loss (gain) would be recorded by the Company when the value of the share purchase warrants increases (decreases).
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	As a result of this interpretation, the Company has restated its US GAAP net earnings for the year ended December 31, 2005 and the four months ended December 31, 2004 to reflect the mark-to-market impacts related to fair valuation of these series of warrants. &nbsp;The restatement has no effect on the Company&#146;s cash flows or liquidity at the ends of the respective restated periods.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	An analysis of this non-cash restatement to US GAAP is as follows:
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Financial Accounting Standards Board (&#147;FASB&#148;) has recently initiated a project on a similar issue to provide implementation guidance on determining whether a conversion option in convertible debt issued with a conversion option that has an exercise price that is denominated in a currency other than the issuer&#146;s functional currency qualifies for the scope exception provided in SFAS 133. &nbsp;This would indicate that the accounting for the issue that gave rise to the Company&#146;s amendment relating to its outstanding share purchase warrants may be revisited by the FASB. &nbsp;&nbsp;
</P>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
	The Company has three business segments, the Luismin contract, the Zinkgruvan contract and corporate operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:22.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	Luismin
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	On October 15, 2004, a 100% subsidiary of the Company, Silver Wheaton (Caymans) Ltd. (&#147;SW Caymans&#148;), entered into an agreement to purchase all of the silver produced by Goldcorp&#146;s Luismin mining operations in Mexico. &nbsp;During 2005, SW Caymans purchased 7.9 million ounces (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; 1.4 million ounces) of silver under the contract at a total cash cost of $3.90 per ounce, and sold it for an average price of $7.28 per ounce (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $7.34 per ounce). &nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s cash flows and net earnings under the Luismin silver contract for 2005 were $26.5 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $4.8 million) and $23.7 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $4.2 million), respectively.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During 2005, an aggressive exploration and development program was carried out at Luismin&#146;s San Dimas mine. &nbsp;This program has been successful with deep and on-strike extensions of the central block veins and new discoveries, including the Itzel vein system and the Paula and Nancy veins. &nbsp;At December 31, 2004, the Luismin mines had proven and probable reserves of 40.3 million ounces of silver and inferred resources of 145.6 million ounces of silver. &nbsp;Luismin has historically converted resources into reserves at a rate of approximately 90%. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
	Since October 15, 2004, all silver produced by Luismin has been sold to Silver Wheaton Corp at a price of $3.90 per ounce.&nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On February 13, 2006, Silver Wheaton announced that it has agreed to amend its existing silver purchase agreement in connection with Goldcorp&#146;s plans to substantially increase
<B>
</B>
	its investment in exploration and development at its San Dimas mine in Mexico. &nbsp;As a result of the planned exploration and development at San Dimas, Silver Wheaton and Goldcorp anticipate that additional silver sales will aggregate more than 100 million ounces over the remaining 24 year term of the silver purchase agreement. &nbsp;It is projected that Silver Wheaton&#146;s annual silver sales will increase to approximately 11.5 million ounces for 2006, 2007 and 2008, increasing to 15 million ounces per annum thereafter.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	6
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage12"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Under the existing silver purchase agreement dated October 15, 2004, Silver Wheaton is entitled to purchase all of the silver produced by Goldcorp&#146;s Mexican operations, Luismin, for a per ounce cash payment of the lesser of US$3.90 and the prevailing market price (subject to an inflationary adjustment commencing in 2007). &nbsp;Further, Luismin is required to deliver a minimum of 120 million ounces over the 25 year contract period and Silver Wheaton is obligated to pay 50% of any capital expenditures made by Luismin at its mining operations in excess of 110% of the projected capital expenditures outlined in the agreement.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Goldcorp and Silver Wheaton have agreed to amend the existing agreement, increasing the minimum number of ounces of silver to be delivered over the 25 year contract period by 100 million ounces, to 220 million ounces, and waiving any capital expenditure contributions previously required to be paid by Silver Wheaton. &nbsp;In consideration for these amendments, Silver Wheaton will issue to Goldcorp 18 million common shares representing 9.8% of the outstanding shares of Silver Wheaton, and a US$20 million promissory note, increasing Goldcorp&#146;s ownership to 62%, or 126 million common shares of Silver Wheaton. &nbsp;Goldcorp does not have any present intention to acquire ownership of, or control over, any additional securities of Silver Wheaton. The total consideration of US$150 million is equal to the approximate value of Silver Wheaton&#146;s share of the future capital expenditures estimated over the remaining life of the existing agreement.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Production of silver at the Luismin mines, which in 2005 approximated 8 million ounces, is expected to average approximately 9.5 million ounces for 2006, 2007 and 2008, increasing to 13 million ounces per annum thereafter. As a result of the amendment to the silver purchase agreement, Silver Wheaton will not be required to fund its 50% share of the increased capital expenditures planned by Goldcorp and will preserve its cash resources to fund growth opportunities.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:22.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	Zinkgruvan
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	On December 8, 2004, SW Caymans entered into an agreement to purchase all of the silver produced by Lundin Mining&#146;s Zinkgruvan mining operations in Sweden (&#147;Zinkgruvan&#148;). During 2005, SW Caymans purchased 1.7 million ounces (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; 0.2 million ounces) of silver under the contract at a total cash cost of $3.90 per ounce, and sold 1.8 million ounces (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; 0.1 million ounces) for an average price of $7.43 per ounce (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $6.89 per ounce). &nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s cash flows and net earnings under the Zinkgruvan silver contract for 2005 were $4.3 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $0.4 million) and $3.3 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $0.1 million), respectively.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	As at December 31, 2004, Zinkgruvan had proven and probable silver reserves of 28.7 million ounces, measured and indicated resources of 8.1 million ounces and inferred silver resources of 27.5 million ounces. &nbsp;The Zinkgruvan mine is expected to produce approximately 2 million ounces of silver annually for a minimum of 20 years, and is one of the lowest cost zinc mines in the world. The mine is located in south-central Sweden and has been in production on a continuous basis since 1857.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	General and administrative expenses totaled $1,980,000 during 2005 (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; $381,000), including $416,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $131,800) paid to Goldcorp for management and administrative services at cost. Also included in general and administrative expenses were professional service fees, including legal, accounting and audit fees, totaling $415,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $100,000), salary expenses of $312,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $nil), and investor relations and regulatory fees of $254,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $54,000). Total general and administrative expenses for the twelve months ended December 31, 2005 were higher than for the four months ended December 31, 2004, because of a full year of operations in 2005 compared to the four month period ended December 31, 2004 for which substantial operations did not commence until October 15, 2004.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The non-cash stock based compensation expense has been estimated using the Black-Scholes option valuation method to determine the fair value of the share purchase options granted. &nbsp;&nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Interest income during 2005 of $705,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $255,000) was the result of interest on cash balances held in short-term money market instruments.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Project evaluation expenses of $91,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $69,000) were incurred in pursuing additional silver acquisition opportunities. &nbsp;Project evaluation expenses will continue to be incurred for the foreseeable future.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During 2005, a foreign exchange gain of $64,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $2,687,000) was realized, as a result of the Company holding a portion of its cash balances in Canadian dollars, while the Canadian dollar increased in value against the US dollar (the Company&#146;s functional currency).
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:22.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">

<B>
	Non GAAP measures &#150; total cash costs per ounce of silver calculation
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Silver Wheaton has included, throughout this document, certain non-GAAP performance measures including total cash costs of silver on a sales basis. &nbsp;These non-GAAP measures do not have any standardized meaning nor are they necessarily comparable with similar measures presented by other companies. &nbsp;Cash costs are presented as they represent an industry standard method of comparing certain costs on a per unit basis. &nbsp;The Company believes that certain investors use this information to evaluate the Company&#146;s performance. &nbsp;The data is intended to provide additional information and should not be considered in isolation or as a substitute for measures of performance prepared in accordance with GAAP. &nbsp;During 2005, the Company&#146;s total cash costs were $3.90 per ounce of silver.
</FONT>

<A NAME="eolPage14"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<B>
	LIQUIDITY AND CAPITAL RESOURCES
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	At December 31, 2005 the Company had cash and cash equivalents of $117.7 million (December 31, 2004 - $20.0 million) and working capital of $118.7 million (December 31, 2004 - $18.1 million).
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During 2005, the Company generated operating cash flows of $30.0 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $8.4 million). &nbsp;In the opinion of management, the working capital at December 31, 2005, together with cash flows from operations, are sufficient to support the Company&#146;s normal operating requirements on an ongoing basis.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During the year ended December 31, 2005, the Company received proceeds of $2.0 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $nil) from the exercise of 710,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; nil) share purchase options at a weighted average exercise price of Cdn$3.27 per option. &nbsp;As of February 13, 2006, there were 183,761,000 outstanding common shares, 6,042,300 share purchase options and 165,620,000 share purchase warrants, which are convertible into 39,374,200 shares.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Public offering
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 22, 2005, the Company raised gross proceeds of $86.2 million (Cdn$100.0 million) from a public offering of 15,625,000 subscription receipts at a price of Cdn$6.40 per unit. &nbsp;Each of the subscription receipts was automatically converted without payment of additional consideration into one common share, and one-half of one Series &#147;B&#148; warrant (TSX: SLW.WT.B) of the Company. Each Series B warrant entitles the holder to purchase one common share at a price of Cdn$10.00 per share for a period of 5 years expiring December 22, 2010. &nbsp;Share issue costs amounted to $4.3 million.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Investment in Bear Creek
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On August 11, 2005, the Company acquired 4,821,905 common shares of Bear Creek Mining Corporation (TSXV: BCM) on the open market at a price of Cdn$3.03 per share, for total consideration of $12.2 million (Cdn$14.6 million). &nbsp;&nbsp;In addition, on August 30, 2005, the Company acquired by way of private placement, 540,000 units of Bear Creek at a price of Cdn$3.25 per unit for total consideration of $1.5 million (Cdn$1.8 million). &nbsp;The units are comprised of one common share and one-half of one common share purchase warrant.&nbsp; Each whole warrant entitles the holder to purchase one common share of Bear Creek at a price of Cdn$4.25 for a period of two years from the transaction close date.&nbsp; As a result, Silver Wheaton owns approximately 15% of Bear Creek&#146;s total issued and outstanding shares.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Bear Creek is earning a 70% interest in the Corani silver project in Peru through continued expenditures and payments. &nbsp;To date, 24 trenches and over 80 drillholes have outlined significant silver mineralization over a large surface area, with a resource estimate expected in Q1 2006. &nbsp;Bear Creek is continuing to advance the project with drilling, environmental and social studies, and metallurgical testing programs.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Contractual obligations
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In connection with the Luismin and Zinkgruvan Transactions, the Company has committed to purchase 100% of the silver produced by each mine for a per-ounce cash payment of the lesser of $3.90 and the then prevailing market price, subject to adjustment. &nbsp;This inflationary adjustment, which will begin in 2007, is intended to reflect the effects of inflation on operating costs, and is subject to a minimum of 0.4% and a maximum of 1.65% per annum. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Discontinued operations
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Effective February 25, 2004, the Company sold its subsidiary, Dial, for cash proceeds of Cdn$325,000 to a group that included former directors and shareholders of the Company.
</P>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
<I>
	Related party transactions
</I>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	At December 31, 2005, Goldcorp owned 58.9% of the Company&#146;s outstanding common shares. &nbsp;During 2005, the Company purchased 7.9 million ounces (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; 1.4 million ounces) of silver from a subsidiary of Goldcorp at a price of $3.90 per ounce for total consideration of approximately $30.8 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $5.4 million). &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company has an agreement with Goldcorp whereby Goldcorp provides management and administrative services at cost. &nbsp;During the year ended December 31, 2005, total management fees paid to Goldcorp were $416,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $131,800). This agreement allows for cancellation with 30 days notice at any time.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In addition, during 2005, payments made by Goldcorp on the Company&#146;s behalf totalled approximately $225,600 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $1.5 million). &nbsp;At December 31, 2005, the Company did not have any outstanding amounts due to Goldcorp (December 31, 2004 - $1.0 million was owed to Goldcorp).
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:7.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:7.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	RISKS AND UNCERTAINTIES
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	The main risks that can affect the profitability of the Company include changes in silver prices, currency fluctuations, government regulation, silver supply, foreign operations and income taxes.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Silver prices
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Profitability of the Company depends on silver prices. A $0.50 per ounce change in the price of silver would impact 2006 net earnings by approximately $6 million.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Silver prices are affected by numerous factors such as the sale or purchase of silver by various central banks and financial institutions, interest rates, exchange rates, inflation or deflation, fluctuations in the value of the US dollar and foreign currencies, global and regional supply and demand, and the political and economic conditions of major silver producing countries throughout the world. This risk is mitigated through the downside silver price protection provided for in the silver contracts, whereby silver is purchased at the lower of $3.90 per ounce or the market price.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Currency fluctuations
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Exchange rate fluctuations may affect the costs that the Company incurs in its operations. Silver is sold in US dollars and a portion of the Company&#146;s costs are incurred in Canadian dollars. From time to time, the Company transacts currency hedging to reduce the risk associated with currency fluctuations. &nbsp;There is no assurance that its hedging strategies will be successful. Currency hedging may require margin activities. Sudden fluctuations in currencies could result in margin calls that could have an adverse effect on the Company&#146;s financial position.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Government regulations
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The mining, processing, development and mineral exploration activities of the companies that Silver Wheaton purchases silver from are subject to various laws governing prospecting, development, production, taxes, labour standards and occupational health, mine safety, toxic substances, land use, water use, land claims of local people and other matters. No assurance can be given that new rules and regulations will not be enacted or that existing rules and regulations will not be applied in a manner which could result in production disturbances.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	10
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage16"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
<I>
	Silver supply
</I>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company has agreed to purchase all of the silver produced by the Luismin and Zinkgruvan mines. &nbsp;Other than the security interests which have been granted to Silver Wheaton, the Company has no contractual rights relating to the operations of Luismin or Zinkgruvan nor does it have any ownership interest in the mines. Other than the penalties payable by Goldcorp &nbsp;and Zinkgruvan to Silver Wheaton if, at the end of the Luismin or Zinkgruvan Guarantee Period, as applicable, the total number of ounces of silver sold to Silver Wheaton is less than the applicable minimum amount, the Company will not be entitled to any compensation if Luismin or Zinkgruvan does not meet its forecasted silver production targets in any specified period or if Luismin or Zinkgruvan shut down or discontinue their mining operations in Mexico and Sweden, respectively, on a temporary or permanent basis.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Foreign operations
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	SW Caymans purchases silver from companies that operate in Mexico and Sweden, and as such the Company&#146;s operations are exposed to various levels of political, economic and other risks and uncertainties. These risks and uncertainties vary between the two countries and include, but are not limited to, terrorism; hostage taking; military repression; extreme fluctuations in currency exchange rates; high rates of inflation; labour unrest; the risk of war or civil unrest; expropriation and nationalization; renegotiation or nullification of existing concessions, licenses, permits and contracts; illegal mining; changes in taxation policies; restrictions on foreign exchange and repatriation; and changing political conditions, currency controls and governmental regulations that favour or require the awarding of contracts to local contractors or require foreign contractors to employ citizens of, or purchase supplies from, a particular jurisdiction.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Failure for these companies to comply strictly with applicable laws, regulations and local practices relating to mineral right applications and tenure, could result in loss, reduction or expropriation of entitlements.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The occurrence of these various factors and uncertainties cannot be accurately predicted and could have an adverse effect on the Company&#146;s operations or profitability.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Income taxes
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	All of the Company&#146;s silver trading activities are performed by it&#146;s wholly owned subsidiary Silver Wheaton (Caymans) Ltd., which is not subject to income taxes. &nbsp;Changes to taxations laws in either Canada or the Cayman Islands, could result in some or all of the Company&#146;s profits being subject to income tax. No assurance can be given that new taxation rules will not be enacted or that existing rules will not be applied in a manner which could result in the Company&#146;s profits being subject to income tax.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:14.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:14.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.

<A NAME="eolPage17"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:14.667PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000">
<B>
	CRITICAL ACCOUNTING ESTIMATES
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	The preparation of financial statements in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amount of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent liabilities at the date of the financial statements, and the reported amounts of revenues and expenditures during the reporting period. Note 2 of the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements describes all of the significant accounting policies.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Silver contracts
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:7.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Silver contracts are a significant asset of the Company, with a carrying value of $130.3 million at December 31, 2005. This amount represents the capitalized expenditures related to the acquisition of the Luismin and Zinkgruvan silver purchase contracts. &nbsp;Luismin and Zinkgruvan estimate the reserves and resources relating to each contract. &nbsp;Silver Wheaton uses these estimates to determine the estimated number of ounces that will be acquired from each operation and the cost of these assets is separately allocated to reserves, resources and exploration potential. &nbsp;The value allocated to reserves is depreciated on a unit-of-sale basis over the estimated recoverable reserves at the mine corresponding to the specific contract. Evaluations of the carrying values of each contract are undertaken in each reporting period to determine if estimated undiscounted future net cash flows are less than the carrying value. &nbsp;Estimated undiscounted future net cash flows are calculated using estimated production, sales prices and purchase costs. &nbsp;If it is determined that the future net cash flows from an operation are less than the carrying value then a write-down is recorded with a charge to operations. &nbsp;At December 31, 2005 no write-down was required.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Luismin Transaction resulted in the acquisition of control of Silver Wheaton by Goldcorp. As a result, the cost of the Luismin silver contract has been recorded in Silver Wheaton&#146;s books at Goldcorp&#146;s book value.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Income tax
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	As the Company&#146;s profit is derived from its subsidiary, Silver Wheaton (Caymans) Ltd., which is incorporated and operated in the Cayman Islands, the Company&#146;s profits bear no tax. Management views the subsidiary&#146;s profits as part of its permanent investment in the subsidiary, and it has determined that those profits will be reinvested in foreign jurisdictions for the foreseeable future, therefore, no taxes have been recorded.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:72PX; TEXT-INDENT:-72PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Revenue recognition
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Revenue from the sale of silver is recognized in the accounts when title and risk passes to the buyer, collection is reasonably assured and the price is reasonably determinable. &nbsp;Revenue from the sale of silver may be subject to adjustment upon final settlement of estimated metal prices, weights, and assays. &nbsp;Adjustments to revenue for metal prices are recorded monthly and other adjustments are recorded on final settlement.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<EFX_CONTROL_AND_PROCEDURES>
<A NAME="FIS_CONTROL_AND_PROCEDURES"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:7.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<B>
	DISCLOSURE CONTROLS AND PROCEDURES
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	The Company&#146;s management, with the participation of its Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, have evaluated the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures. Based upon the results of that evaluation, the Company&#146;s Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer have concluded that, as of the end of the period covered by this report, the Company&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures were effective to provide reasonable assurance that the information required to be disclosed by the Company in reports it files is recorded, processed, summarized and reported, within the appropriate time periods and forms. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s management, including the Chief Executive Officer and Chief Financial Officer, believe that any disclosure controls and procedures or internal controls and procedures, no matter how well conceived and operated, can provide only reasonable, not absolute, assurance that the objectives of the control system are met. Further, the design of a control system must reflect the fact that there are resource constraints, and the benefits of controls must be considered relative to their costs. Because of the inherent limitations in all control systems, they cannot provide absolute assurance that all control issues and instances of fraud, if any, within the Company have been prevented or detected. These inherent limitations include the realities that judgments in decision-making can be faulty, and that breakdowns can occur because of simple error or mistake. Additionally, controls can be circumvented by the individual acts of some persons, by collusion of two or more people, or by unauthorized override of the control. The design of any systems of controls also is based in part upon certain assumptions about the likelihood of future events, and there can be no assurance that any design will succeed in achieving its stated goals under all potential future conditions. Accordingly, because of the inherent limitations in a cost effective control system, misstatements due to error or fraud may occur and not be detected. There has been no change in the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting during the Company&#146;s quarter ended September 30, 2006 that has materially affected, or is reasonably likely to materially affect, the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:24.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000">

<EFX_AUDITORS_OPINION>
<A NAME="FIS_AUDITORS_OPINION"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.267PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX">
<B>
	Report of Independent Registered Chartered Accountants
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	To the Shareholders of
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
	Silver Wheaton Corp.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	We have audited the consolidated balance sheets of Silver Wheaton Corp. as at December 31, 2005, December 31, 2004, and August 31, 2004 and the consolidated statements of operations, shareholders&#146; equity and cash flows for the year ended December 31, 2005, the four month period ended December&nbsp;31, 2004 and the years ended August 31, 2004 and 2003. &nbsp;These financial statements are the responsibility of the Company's management. &nbsp;Our responsibility is to express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	We conducted our audits in accordance with Canadian generally accepted auditing standards and the standards of the United States Public Company Accounting Oversight Board. &nbsp;Those standards require that we plan and perform an audit to obtain reasonable assurance whether the financial statements are free of material misstatement. &nbsp;An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements. &nbsp;An audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial statement presentation. &nbsp;We believe that our audits provide a reasonable basis for our opinion.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In our opinion, these consolidated financial statements present fairly, in all material respects, the financial position of Silver Wheaton Corp. &nbsp;as at December 31, 2005, December 31, 2004 and August 31, 2004 and the results of its operations and its cash flows for the year ended December 31, 2005, the four month period ended December 31, 2004 and the years ended August 31, 2004 and 2003 in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	We have withdrawn our audit report dated March 3, 2006 as Note 13 to the consolidated financial statements has been restated. &nbsp;Note 13 &nbsp;contains the reconciliation of the consolidated financial statements from Canadian generally accepted accounting principles to accounting principles generally accepted in the United States and contains additional information on the restatement.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:15.867PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company is not required to have, nor were we engaged to perform, an audit of its internal control over financial reporting. &nbsp;Our audit included consideration of internal control over financial reporting as a basis for designing audit procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an opinion on the effectiveness of the Company&#146;s internal control over financial reporting. &nbsp;Accordingly we express no such opinion.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>

</P>

<A NAME="eolPage25"></A>

	Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:18.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:16PX">
	Year Ended December 31, 2005, Four Months Ended December 31, 2004 and Years Ended August 31, 2004 and 2003
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:13.333PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-BOTTOM:4PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC; FONT-SIZE:10.667PX; BORDER-BOTTOM:1PX SOLID #000000">

<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-16PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<B>
	1.

</EFX_NOTES_TO_FINANCIAL_STATEMENT>
<EFX_BUSINESS>
<A NAME="FIS_BUSINESS"></A>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<B>
	DESCRIPTION OF BUSINESS AND NATURE OF OPERATIONS
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Silver Wheaton Corp. (&#147;Silver Wheaton&#148; or &#147;the Company&#148;) is engaged in the silver mining business. &nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On October 15, 2004, the Company entered into an agreement to purchase all of the silver produced by Wheaton River Minerals Ltd&#146;s (&#147;Wheaton River&#148;) Luismin mining operations in Mexico for a payment equal to the lesser of US$3.90 or the prevailing market rate per ounce of delivered silver, subject to adjustment (Note 3). &nbsp;On April 15, 2005, Wheaton River amalgamated with Goldcorp Inc. to form Goldcorp Inc. (&#147;Goldcorp&#148;) and the silver purchase agreement with Silver Wheaton was assumed by Goldcorp.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In addition, on December 8, 2004, the Company entered into an agreement to purchase all of the silver produced by Lundin Mining Corporation&#146;s Zinkgruvan mine in Sweden for a payment equal to the lesser of US$3.90 or the prevailing market rate per ounce of delivered silver, subject to adjustment (Note 3).
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company began trading on the Toronto Stock Exchange (TSX) on October 22, 2004 and on the American Stock Exchange (AMEX) on July 6, 2005, under the symbol SLW. In December, 2004, the Company&#146;s name was changed from Chap Mercantile Inc to Silver Wheaton Corp. and the outstanding shares were consolidated on a 5 for 1 basis. The year end of the Company was changed
<A NAME="SILVERWHEATONFORM40FA2005_HTM_OLE_LINK1">
</A>
<A NAME="SILVERWHEATONFORM40FA2005_HTM_OLE_LINK2">
</A>
	from August 31 to December 31 and as a result, the comparative figures are for the four months ended December 31, 2004 and the years ended August 31, 2004 and 2003.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-16PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	2.
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	ACCOUNTING POLICIES
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
<I>
	&nbsp;(a)
</I>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Canadian generally accepted accounting principles
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	These consolidated financial statements have been prepared in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles (&#147;GAAP&#148;). A reconciliation of Canadian GAAP and accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;US GAAP&#148;) is provided in Note 13.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(b)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Principles of consolidation
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of the Company and its 100% owned subsidiary Silver Wheaton (Caymans) Ltd. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s former subsidiary, Dial Locksmith Ltd (&#147;Dial&#148;), was consolidated to the date of disposal, February 25, 2004.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:1.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(c)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Silver contracts
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.2PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Contracts for which settlement is called for in silver are recorded at cost. &nbsp;The cost of these assets is separately allocated to reserves, resources and exploration potential. &nbsp;The value allocated to reserves is depreciated on a unit-of-sale basis over the estimated recoverable reserves at the mine corresponding to the specific contract.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.2PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Evaluations of the carrying values of each contract are undertaken in each reporting period to determine if estimated undiscounted future net cash flows are less than the carrying value. &nbsp;Estimated undiscounted future net cash flows are calculated using estimated production, sales prices and purchase costs. &nbsp;If it is determined that the future net cash flows from an operation are less than the carrying value then a write-down is recorded with a charge to operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	20
</B>
</P>

<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage26"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:71.8PX; TEXT-INDENT:-23.8PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
<I>
	(d)
</I>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:71.8PX; TEXT-INDENT:24.2PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Discontinued operations
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company disposed of Dial effective February 25, 2004.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(e)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Change in functional and reporting currency
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Effective September 1, 2004, the functional currency of the Company was changed from the Canadian to the United States dollar. This resulted from a change in the nature of the business as all sales and the majority of expenses occur in United States dollars. &nbsp;Concurrent with this change in functional currency, the Company adopted the United States dollar as its reporting currency. In accordance with Canadian GAAP, the change was effected by translating assets and liabilities, at the end of prior reporting periods, at the existing United States / Canadian dollar foreign exchange spot rate, while earnings, losses and shareholders&#146; equity were translated at historic rates. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(f)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Foreign currency translation
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Foreign currency monetary assets and liabilities are translated into United States dollars at the exchange rates prevailing at the balance sheet date. &nbsp;Non-monetary assets denominated in foreign currencies are translated using the rate of exchange at the transaction date. &nbsp;Foreign currency transactions are translated at the United States dollar rate prevailing on the transaction dates. Foreign exchange gains and losses are included in the determination of earnings.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(g)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Income taxes
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The future income tax asset and liability method of accounting for income taxes is used. &nbsp;As the Company&#146;s profit is derived from its subsidiary, Silver Wheaton (Caymans) Ltd., which is incorporated and operated in the Cayman Islands, the Company&#146;s profits bear no tax. Management views the subsidiary&#146;s profits as part of its permanent investment in the subsidiary, and it has determined that those profits will be reinvested in foreign jurisdictions for the foreseeable future, therefore, no taxes have been recorded.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(h)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Use of estimates
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The preparation of financial statements in conformity with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities as at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. &nbsp;Significant areas where management&#146;s judgment is applied are asset valuations, depreciation, and income taxes. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from those reported.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(i)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Stock-based compensation
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The fair value of all stock-based awards granted are estimated using the Black-Scholes model and are recorded in operations. &nbsp;The compensation cost related to stock options granted to employees and directors is recorded in the consolidated statements of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company did not issue stock options prior to the year ended August&nbsp;31, 2003.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(j)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Financial instruments
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The carrying values of cash and cash equivalents, marketable securities, accounts receivable, accounts payable and accrued liabilities approximate their fair values due to their short term nature. &nbsp;Unless otherwise noted, it is management's opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency or credit risk arising from these financial instruments.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>

</B>

<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage27"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:1.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
<I>
	(k)
</I>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Long-term investments
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Long-term investments are carried at cost. When there is decline in market value that is other than temporary, these investments are written down to provide for the loss.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:1.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(l)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Revenue recognition
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.2PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Revenue from the sale of silver is recognized in the accounts when title and risk passes to the buyer, collection is reasonably assured and the price is reasonably determinable. &nbsp;Revenue from the sale of silver may be subject to adjustment upon final settlement of estimated metal prices, weights, and assays. &nbsp;Adjustments to revenue for metal prices are recorded monthly and other adjustments are recorded on final settlement.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:1.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(m)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Earnings per share
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.2PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Earnings per share calculations are based on the weighted average number of common shares and common share equivalents issued and outstanding during the period. Diluted earnings per share are calculated using the treasury method which requires the calculation of diluted earnings per share by assuming that outstanding share purchase options and warrants, with an average market price that exceeds the average exercise prices of the options and warrants for the year, are exercised and the proceeds are used to repurchase shares of the Company at the average market price of the common shares for the period.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:1.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(n)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Cash and cash equivalents
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.2PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Cash and cash equivalents include cash, and those short-term money market instruments that are readily convertible to cash with an original term to maturity of less than 91 days.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:1.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	(o)
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Silver inventory
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.133PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Silver inventory is valued at the lower of average cost and net realizable value.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-16PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	3.
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	ACQUISITIONS
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	(a)
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; TEXT-INDENT:48.933PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
<I>
	Luismin silver contract
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:94.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On October 15, 2004, the Company entered into a twenty five year agreement to purchase all of the silver produced by Goldcorp&#146;s Luismin mining operations in Mexico, for an upfront payment of $36.7 million (Cdn$46.0&nbsp;million) in cash and 108 million common shares (post-consolidation) of the Company. In addition, a per ounce cash payment of the lesser of $3.90 and the prevailing market price, subject to adjustment, is due (the &#147;Luismin Transaction&#148;). &nbsp;Under the agreement Luismin is required to deliver a minimum of 120 million ounces over the 25 year period following the contract date. &nbsp;If the actual amount of silver delivered is less than this minimum, a penalty of $0.50 per ounce of the shortfall is payable. In addition, under the agreement, Silver Wheaton will be obligated to pay 50% of any capital expenditures made by Luismin at its mining operations in excess of 110% of the projected capital expenditures outlined in the contract, however, these costs will be reimbursed during periods where actual capital expenditures fall below 90% of projected capital expenditures.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	22
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage28"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:94.867PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	If Silver Wheaton or Goldcorp acquires a direct or indirect interest in a precious metal exploration or development property situated anywhere in Mexico, which it does not currently own an interest in, and the property becomes the subject of a positive feasibility study or consists of active mining operations within a period of three years from the date of the contract, then the owner of the interest must offer the other party the opportunity to purchase and participate in the project so the resulting project ownership would be Goldcorp 51% / Silver Wheaton 49% and Goldcorp will be entitled to become operator of the project.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:95.067PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.933PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	For a period of three years, Goldcorp, so long as it owns at least 20% of the outstanding shares of the Company, has the right to maintain its pro-rata interest in Silver Wheaton should Silver Wheaton issue any additional Silver Wheaton shares pursuant to an equity financing or otherwise.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:95.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

	The Luismin Transaction resulted in the acquisition of control of Silver Wheaton by Goldcorp. As a result, the cost of the Luismin silver contract was recorded in Silver Wheaton&#146;s books at Goldcorp&#146;s book value, plus acquisition costs of $430,000.

	(b)
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<I>
	Zinkgruvan silver contract
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 8, 2004, the Company entered into an agreement to purchase all of the silver produced by Lundin Mining Corporation&#146;s Zinkgruvan mine in Sweden for an upfront payment of $50 million in cash, 6 million Silver Wheaton common shares (post-consolidation) and 30 million Silver Wheaton common share purchase warrants. In addition, a per ounce cash payment of the lesser of $3.90 and the prevailing market price, subject to adjustment, is due (the &#147;Zinkgruvan Transaction&#148;). &nbsp;Under the agreement Zinkgruvan is required to deliver a minimum of 40 million ounces over the 25 year period following the contract date. &nbsp;If the actual amount of silver delivered is less than this minimum, a penalty of $1.00 per ounce of the shortfall is payable. In addition, under the Zinkgruvan agreement, the Company is not liable for any capital asset expenditures. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Each warrant grants the holder the right to purchase 0.20 of one of the Company&#146;s post-consolidation common shares. The Warrants have been recorded at their fair value, which has been determined using the Black-Scholes option pricing model assuming no dividends are to be paid, a weighted average volatility of the Company&#146;s share price of 40%, an annual risk free interest rate of 3.0% and expected lives of three years.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On August 11, 2005, the Company acquired 4,821,905 common shares of Bear Creek Mining Corporation (TSXV: BCM) (&#147;Bear Creek&#148;) on the open market at a price of Cdn$3.03 per share, for total consideration of $12.2 million (Cdn$14.6 million). &nbsp;&nbsp;In addition, on August 30, 2005, the Company acquired by way of private placement, 540,000 units of Bear Creek at a price of Cdn$3.25 per unit for total consideration of $1.5 million (Cdn$1.8 million). &nbsp;The units are comprised of one common share and one-half of one common share purchase warrant.&nbsp; Each whole warrant entitles the holder to purchase one common share of Bear Creek at a price of Cdn$4.25 for a period of two years from the transaction close date.&nbsp; As a result, Silver Wheaton owns approximately 15% of Bear Creek&#146;s total issued and outstanding shares. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.267PX; TEXT-INDENT:0.733PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The market value of Bear Creek includes the estimated value of the warrants acquired as part of the private placement, which have been valued using a binomial option pricing model.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">

<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	5.
</B>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On August 5, 2004, in connection with the Luismin Transaction, the Company raised gross proceeds of $53.2 million (Cdn$70 million) from a private placement of 175 million subscription receipts at a price of Cdn$0.40 per unit. On October 22, 2004, each of the subscription receipts was automatically converted without payment of additional consideration into 0.2 common shares (post-consolidation), and one-half of one common share purchase warrant of the Company (TSX: SLW.WT). Five common share purchase warrants entitle the holder to purchase one common share (post-consolidation) at a price of Cdn$4.00 per share for a period of five years expiring August 5, 2009. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On November 30, 2004, in connection with the Zinkgruvan Transaction, the Company raised gross proceeds of $51.0 million (Cdn$60.75 million) from a private placement of 81 million subscription receipts at a price of Cdn$0.75 per unit. &nbsp;Each subscription receipt was automatically converted without payment of additional consideration into 0.2 Silver Wheaton common shares (post-consolidation) and one-half of one Series &#147;A&#148; common share purchase warrant &nbsp;(TSX: SLW.WT.A) of Silver Wheaton. Five Series &#147;A&#148; warrants entitle the holder to purchase one Silver Wheaton common share (post-consolidation) at a price of Cdn$5.50 until November 30, 2009. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 21, 2004 the Company&#146;s common shares were consolidated on a 5 for 1 basis, reducing the number of common shares outstanding at December 31, 2004 to 167,010,000.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

</FONT>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	At issuance, each share purchase warrant and Series A warrant (TSX: SLW.WT and SLW.WT.A respectively) granted the holder the right to purchase one common share of the Company at the applicable exercise price. On December 21, 2004, the Company&#146;s common shares were consolidated 5 for 1. &nbsp;These warrants were not consolidated, resulting in each warrant granting the holder the right to purchase 0.20 of one of the Company&#146;s post-consolidation common shares. &nbsp;The Series B warrants were issued after the December 21, 2004 share consolidation, and therefore, each Series B warrant entitles the holder the right to purchase one of the Company&#146;s post-consolidation common shares.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Warrants issued during the year ended December 31, 2005 and the four months ended December 31, 2004 have been included in shareholders&#146; equity at their fair value of $10.3 million and$28.6 million, respectively. Fair value of the warrants issued during 2005 has been determined using the Black-Scholes option pricing model assuming no dividends are to be paid, a weighted average volatility of the Company&#146;s share price of 40%, an annual risk free interest rate of 3.0% and expected lives of five years.
</P>

<I>
	Share purchase options
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company has established a share purchase option plan whereby the Company&#146;s board of directors may from time to time grant options to directors, employees or consultants. The maximum term of any option may be ten years, but generally options are granted for five years or less. &nbsp;The exercise price of an option is not less than the closing price on the TSX on the last trading day preceding the grant date. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Stock-based compensation expense during 2005 of $463,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $5,046,000) was determined using an option pricing model assuming no dividends are to be paid, a weighted average volatility of the Company&#146;s share price of 40%, an annual risk free interest rate of 3.0% and expected lives of three years.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On December 21, 2004 the Company&#146;s common shares were consolidated on a 5 for 1 basis, therefore, all of the option figures below are presented on a consolidated basis. &nbsp;At December 31, 2005 there were 4,330,000 options available for grant under the plan.
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	RELATED PARTY TRANSACTIONS
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	At December 31, 2005, Goldcorp owned 58.9% of the Company&#146;s outstanding common shares. &nbsp;During 2005, the Company purchased 7.9 million ounces (four months ended December 31, 2004 &#150; 1.4 million ounces) of silver from a subsidiary of Goldcorp at a price of $3.90 per ounce for total consideration of approximately $30.8 million (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $5.4 million). &nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The Company has an agreement with Goldcorp whereby Goldcorp provides management and administrative services at cost. &nbsp;During the year ended December 31, 2005, total management fees paid to Goldcorp were $416,000 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $131,800). This agreement allows for cancellation with 30 days notice at any time.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.133PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In addition, during 2005, payments made by Goldcorp on the Company&#146;s behalf totalled approximately $225,600 (four months ended December 31, 2004 - $1.5 million). &nbsp;At December 31, 2005, the Company did not have any outstanding amounts due to Goldcorp (December 31, 2004 - $1.0 million was owed to Goldcorp).
</P>

<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:12PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Prior to the Luismin transaction, the Company operated primarily in Canada and was subject to taxation at the applicable statutory rates. &nbsp;Subsequent to the Luismin transaction, all of the Company&#146;s income generating activities, including the sale of silver, are conducted by its 100% owned subsidiary Silver Wheaton (Caymans) Ltd. &nbsp;(&#147;SW Caymans&#148;). &nbsp;SW Caymans operates in the Cayman Islands and is subject to a statutory tax rate of nil%. &nbsp;The Company does not have any plans to repatriate this money to Canada. &nbsp;As a result, no future income tax assets or liabilities have been recognized.
</P>

<B>
	COMMITMENTS
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	In connection with the Luismin and Zinkgruvan Transactions (Note 3), the Company has committed to purchase 100% of the silver produced by each mine for a per-ounce cash payment of the lesser of $3.90 and the then prevailing market price, subject to adjustment.
</FONT>

	The Company does not have any fixed commitments.
