<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	DISCONTINUED OPERATIONS
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Effective February 25, 2004, the Company sold its subsidiary, Dial, for cash proceeds of $247,000 to a group that included former directors and shareholders of the Company.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The operations of Dial have been accounted for as a discontinued operation and, for reporting purposes, the results of operations, financial position and cash flows have been segregated from those of continuing operations for the current and prior periods. &nbsp;The Company has included in the results of discontinued operations the loss on the sale of Dial and the earnings from discontinued operations from the measurement date to the disposal date. &nbsp;At December 31, 2005 and 2004 and August 31, 2004 the Company did not have any assets or liabilities pertaining to discontinued operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:47.067PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>

<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:87.533PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	(a)
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:87.533PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	For Canadian GAAP purposes, share purchase warrants are classified and accounted for as equity in the Company&#146;s financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	32
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage38"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:87.533PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	The technical interpretation by US regulatory authorities of US GAAP, in accordance with SFAS 133, &nbsp;
</FONT>
<I>
	Accounting for Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities,
</I>
	requires share purchase warrants with an exercise price denominated in a currency other than the Company&#146;s functional currency be classified and accounted for as a financial liability at their fair value with any resulting gains or losses being included in the calculation of US GAAP earnings. &nbsp;As a result of this interpretation, the Company has restated its December 31, 2005 and 2004 US GAAP net earnings to reflect the mark-to-market impacts related to fair valuation of the Company&#146;s warrants. &nbsp;The net effect of the restatement is to reduce net earnings in 2005 by an amount of $50.1 million arising from the recognition of a mark-to-market loss on the share purchase warrants (2004 &#150; mark-to-market loss of $8.0 million). &nbsp;&nbsp;This non-cash restatement has no effect on the Company&#146;s cash flow or liquidity at the ends of the respective restated periods.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:87.533PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	(b)
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:87.533PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Under US GAAP (FAS 115 &#150; Accounting For Certain Investments in Debt and Equity Securities), the Company&#146;s Long-term investments would be classified as available-for-sale securities and carried at fair value. The unrealized holding gains at December 31, 2005 on available-for-sale securities are not recognized under Canadian generally accepted accounting principles, but are recognized under United States accounting principles as a component of comprehensive income and reported as a net amount in a separate component of shareholders&#146; equity until realized.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:6PX; PADDING-LEFT:24PX; TEXT-INDENT:24PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
<I>
	Recently released accounting standards
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX">
	Recently issued United States accounting pronouncements have been outlined below.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In March 2005, the Emerging Issues Committee issued EITF 04-3, Mining Assets &#150; Impairment and Business Combinations, which states that an entity should include Value Beyond Proven and Probable Reserves and Resources (&#147;VBPP&#148;) in the value allocated to mining assets in a purchase price allocation to the extent that a market participant would include VBPP in determining the fair value of the assets. &nbsp;EITF 04-3 also states that an entity should include the effects of anticipated fluctuations in the future market price of minerals in determining the fair value of mining assets in a purchase price allocation in a manner that is consistent with the expectations of marketplace participants. &nbsp;In addition, EITF 04-3 states that an entity should include the cash flows associated with VBPP as well as the effects of anticipated fluctuations in the market price of minerals &nbsp;in estimates of future cash flows (both undiscounted and discounted) used for determining whether a mining asset is impaired. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s current accounting policy of allocating the cost of silver contracts and mining interests separately to reserves, resources and exploration potential and depreciating the value attributed to reserves on a unit-of-sale basis over the estimated recoverable reserves for each specific contract, is in compliance with EITF 04-3.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In November 2005, the FASB issued FASB Staff Position (FSP) FAS 115-1 and FAS 124-1 &#150;
<I>
	The Meaning of Other-Than-Temporary Impairment and Its Application to Certain Investments
</I>
	. &nbsp;This FSP addresses the determination as to when an investment is considered impaired, whether that impairment is other than temporary, and the measurement of an impairment loss. This FSP also includes accounting considerations subsequent to the recognition of an other-than-temporary impairment and requires certain disclosures about unrealized losses that have not been recognized as other-than-temporary impairments. The guidance in this FSP FAS 115-1 and FAS 124-1 is applicable to reporting periods beginning after December 15, 2005. Management does not expect the adoption of this FSP to have a material effect on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial position and results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In December 2004, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (R) &#150;
<I>
	Share-Based Payment
</I>
	, which replaces SFAS No.&nbsp;123&nbsp;&#150;
<I>
	Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation
</I>
	, and supersedes APB Opinion No.&nbsp;25 &#150;
<I>
	Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees
</I>
	. &nbsp;In March 2005, the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) issued Staff Accounting Bulletin No.&nbsp;107 &#150;
<I>
	Share-Based Payment
</I>
	, which provides interpretive guidance related to SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (R). &nbsp;SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (R) requires compensation costs related to share-based payment transactions to be recognized in the financial statements.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	33
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage39"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	With limited exceptions, the amount of compensation cost is measured based on the grant-date fair value of the equity or liability instruments issued. &nbsp;SFAS No.&nbsp;123 (R) requires liability awards to be re-measured each reporting period and compensation costs to be recognized over the period that an employee provides service in exchange for the award. Management plans to adopt this statement on the modified prospective basis beginning January&nbsp;1, 2006, and does not expect adoption of this statement to have a material effect on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial position and results of operations. &nbsp;Subsequent to adoption of this statement, share-based benefits will be valued at fair value using the Black-Scholes option pricing model for option grants and the grant date fair market value for stock awards. Compensation amounts so determined will be expensed over the applicable vesting period.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In March, 2005, the FASB issued FIN 47, &#147;Accounting for Conditional Asset Retirement Obligation &#150; an interpretation of FASB 143&#148;. &nbsp;FIN 47 provides guidance that an entity must record a liability even if the obligation is conditional upon the occurrence of a future event (e.g. plant shutdown), unless it is not possible to make a reasonable estimate of the obligation. &nbsp;It also provides criteria for determining when an asset retirement obligation may be estimated reasonably. &nbsp;The interpretation is effective no later than the end of fiscal years ending after December 15, 2005. &nbsp;Retroactive application for interim financial information is permitted but not required. &nbsp;The Company has adopted this standard which did not have a significant impact on its results of operations. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In May 2005, the FASB issued FAS 154 &#150; Accounting Changes and Error Corrections, a replacement of APB Opinion 20 and FASB Statement 3. This Statement of changes the requirements for the accounting for and reporting a change in accounting principle and applies to all voluntary changes in accounting principle. &nbsp;It also applies to changes required by an accounting pronouncement in the unusual instance that the pronouncement does not include specific transition provisions. &nbsp;The Statement is effective for accounting changes made in fiscal years beginning after December 15, 2005. &nbsp;&nbsp;Management does not expect the adoption of this Statement to have a material effect on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial position and results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	The FASB issued FAS 153- Exchanges of Non-monetary Assets, an amendment of APB Opinion 29. &nbsp;This Statement amends Opinion 29 to eliminate the exception for non-monetary exchanges of similar productive assets and replaces it with a general exception for exchanges of non-monetary assets that do not have commercial substance. &nbsp;A non-monetary exchange has commercial substance if the future cash flows of the entity are expected to change significantly as a result of the exchange. &nbsp;The Statement is effective for fiscal periods beginning after June 15, 2005. &nbsp;Management does not expect the adoption of this Statement to have a material effect on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial position and results of operations.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In November 2005, the FASB concluded that in their proposed Accounting for Uncertain Tax Positions &#150; an Interpretation of FASB Statement No. 109, a benefit recognition model with a two-step approach would be used, with a more-likely-than-not recognition criterion and a best estimate measure attribute. The first step is to evaluate the tax position for recognition by determining if the weight of available evidence indicates it is more-likely-than-not, based solely on the technical merits, that the position will be sustained on audit, including resolution of related appeals or litigation processes, if any.&nbsp; The second step is to measure the appropriate amount of the benefit to recognize, which will be measured using the best estimate of the amount that will be sustained.&nbsp; The tax position should be derecognized when it is no longer more-likely-than-not of being sustained.&nbsp; In January 2006, the FASB concluded that the final Interpretation will be effective as of the beginning of the first annual period beginning after December 31, 2006.&nbsp; The Company is currently evaluating the implications of this Interpretation.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In February 2006, the FASB issued FAS 155 Accounting for Certain Hybrid Financial Instruments &#150; an amendment of FASB Statements No. 133 and 140. This Statement resolves issues addressed in Statement 133 Implementation Issue No. D1, &#147;Application of Statement 133 to Beneficial Interests in Securitized Financial Assets.&#148;&nbsp; &nbsp;This Statement:
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:3PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:SYMBOL; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="SYMBOL">
	&#183;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Permits fair value remeasurement for any hybrid financial instrument that contains an embedded derivative that otherwise would require bifurcation
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:3PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:SYMBOL; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="SYMBOL">
	&#183;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Clarifies which interest-only strips and principal-only strips are not subject to the requirements of Statement 133
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:3PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	34
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage40"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:3PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:SYMBOL; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="SYMBOL">
	&#183;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Establishes a requirement to evaluate interests in securitized financial assets to identify interests that are freestanding derivatives or that are hybrid financial instruments that contain an embedded derivative requiring bifurcation
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:3PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:SYMBOL; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="SYMBOL">
	&#183;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; PADDING-RIGHT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Clarifies that concentrations of credit risk in the form of subordination are not embedded derivatives
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; TEXT-INDENT:-24PX; FONT-FAMILY:SYMBOL; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="SYMBOL">
	&#183;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:96PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Amends Statement 140 to eliminate the prohibition on a qualifying special-purpose entity from holding a derivative financial instrument that pertains to a beneficial interest other than another derivative financial instrument.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	This Statement is effective for all financial instruments acquired or issued after the beginning of fiscal&nbsp;years that begin after September 15, 2006. &nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is currently evaluating the implications of this Statement.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:13.333PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-16PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	14.
</B>
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC">
<B>
	SUBSEQUENT EVENTS
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-27.8PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	(a)
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On February 13, 2006, Silver Wheaton announced that it has agreed to amend its existing silver purchase agreement in connection with Goldcorp&#146;s plans to substantially increase
<B>
</B>
	its investment in exploration and development at its San Dimas mine in Mexico. &nbsp;As a result of the planned exploration and development at San Dimas, Silver Wheaton and Goldcorp anticipate that additional silver sales will aggregate more than 100 million ounces over the remaining 24 year term of the silver purchase agreement. &nbsp;
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Under the existing silver purchase agreement dated October 15, 2004, Silver Wheaton is entitled to purchase all of the silver produced by Goldcorp&#146;s Mexican operations, Luismin, for a per ounce cash payment of the lesser of US$3.90 and the prevailing market price (subject to an inflationary adjustment commencing in 2007). &nbsp;Further, Luismin is required to deliver a minimum of 120 million ounces over the 25 year contract period and Silver Wheaton is obligated to pay 50% of any capital expenditures made by Luismin at its mining operations in excess of 110% of the projected capital expenditures outlined in the agreement.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Goldcorp and Silver Wheaton have agreed to amend the existing agreement, increasing the minimum number of ounces of silver to be delivered over the 25 year contract period by 100 million ounces, to 220 million ounces, and waiving any capital expenditure contributions previously required to be paid by Silver Wheaton. &nbsp;In consideration for these amendments, Silver Wheaton will issue to Goldcorp 18 million common shares representing 9.8% of the outstanding shares of Silver Wheaton, and a US$20 million promissory note, increasing Goldcorp&#146;s ownership to 62%, or 126 million common shares of Silver Wheaton. &nbsp;Goldcorp does not have any present intention to acquire ownership of, or control over, any additional securities of Silver Wheaton. The total consideration of US$150 million is equal to the approximate value of Silver Wheaton&#146;s share of the future capital expenditures estimated over the remaining life of the existing agreement.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Production of silver at the Luismin mines, which in 2005 approximated 8 million ounces, is expected to average approximately 9.5 million ounces for 2006, 2007 and 2008, increasing to 13 million ounces per annum thereafter. As a result of the amendment to the silver purchase agreement, Silver Wheaton will not be required to fund its 50% share of the increased capital expenditures planned by Goldcorp and will preserve its cash resources to fund growth opportunities.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:0PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:14.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:5PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-14.667PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; TEXT-INDENT:-27.8PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	(b)
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:5PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	On February 23, 2006, Silver Wheaton announced that it has agreed to purchase 4.75 million ounces of silver per year, for a period of 20 years, from Glencore International AG, based on the production from their Yauliyacu mining operations in Per&#250;.&nbsp; With this acquisition, Silver Wheaton is expected to have annual silver sales of over 15 million ounces in 2006, increasing to 20 million ounces by 2009 and thereafter.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:5PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:5PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	Silver Wheaton will pay an upfront payment of $285 million, comprised of $245 million in cash and a $40 million promissory note, and $3.90 per ounce of silver delivered under the contract (subject to an inflationary adjustment after three years).
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:5PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.
</FONT>
<B>
	35
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX">
<BR>
</P>
<HR STYLE="MARGIN-TOP:9.6PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:9.6PX" NOSHADE SIZE=1.333>
<A NAME="eolPage41"></A>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:5PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:5PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX; PAGE-BREAK-BEFORE:ALWAYS" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<FONT FACE="GEORGIA">
	Yauliyacu is a low-cost silver/lead/zinc mine located in central Per&#250; which has been in continuous operation for more than 100 years and is expected to produce an average of 6 million ounces of silver per year during the term of the contract. &nbsp;In the event that silver produced at Yauliyacu in any year totals less than 4.75 million ounces, the amount sold to Silver Wheaton in subsequent years will be increased to make up for the shortfall, so long as production allows
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:5PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:5PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	During the term of the contract, Silver Wheaton will have a right of first refusal on any future sales of silver streams from the Yauliyacu mine and a right of first offer on future sales of silver from any other mine currently owned by Glencore. &nbsp;In addition, Silver Wheaton will also have an option to extend the 20 year term of the silver purchase agreement in five year increments, on substantially the same terms as the existing agreement, subject to an adjustment related to silver price expectations at the time and other factors.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:20.667PX; MARGIN-TOP:5PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:5PX; PADDING-LEFT:48PX; FONT-FAMILY:GEORGIA; FONT-SIZE:12PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
	In order to fund the $245 million cash consideration, Silver Wheaton intends to use cash on hand of $120 million, together with $125 million of bank debt. &nbsp;Closing of the transaction is subject to execution of definitive agreements and receipt of all regulatory approvals and third-party consents, including acceptance by the Toronto Stock Exchange.&nbsp; The transaction is expected to close in March 2006.
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:5PX" ALIGN=JUSTIFY>
<BR>
<BR>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0PX; FONT-FAMILY:CENTURY GOTHIC" ALIGN=RIGHT>
<FONT FACE="CENTURY GOTHIC">
	SILVER WHEATON CORP.

<B>
	Cautionary Note to United States Investors Concerning Estimates of Measured, Indicated and Inferred Resources:
</B>
	&nbsp; This news release uses the terms &#147;Measured&#148;, &#147;Indicated&#148; and &#147;Inferred&#148; Resources.&nbsp; United States investors are advised that while such terms are recognized and required by Canadian regulations, the United States Securities and Exchange Commission does not recognize them.&nbsp; &#147;Inferred Mineral Resources&#148; have a great amount of uncertainty as to their existence, and as to their economic and legal feasibility.&nbsp; It cannot be assumed that all or any part of an Inferred Mineral Resource will ever be upgraded to a higher category.&nbsp; Under Canadian rules, estimates of Inferred Mineral Resources may not form the basis of feasibility or other economic studies.&nbsp;
<B>
	United States investors are cautioned not to assume that all or any part of Measured or Indicated Mineral Resources will ever be converted into Mineral Reserves.&nbsp; United States investors are also cautioned not to assume that all or any part of an Inferred Mineral Resource exists, or is economically or legally mineable.
</B>

</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:17.333PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:-17.333PX; TEXT-INDENT:48PX; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX">
	5.
</P>
<P STYLE="LINE-HEIGHT:17.333PX; MARGIN-TOP:0PX; MARGIN-BOTTOM:14.667PX; TEXT-INDENT:96PX; FONT-SIZE:14.667PX">

</P>
